GT Equivalence Verification (BPG8)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4 + c5*P
Candidate formulas: 116

GT (fixed) simplifies to a function of **P only**:
\[
0.9909642091509507\Big((1-\tfrac{P}{39.01184604772507})P + P^{1/3} + P\Big)
= A\,P^{1/3} + 2A\,P - \frac{A}{39.01184604772507}P^2
\]
where \(A=0.9909642091509507\).  
So GT is exactly a linear combination of **three monomials**: \(P^{1/3}, P, P^2\), with **no \(t\)** dependence and **no constant term**.

Therefore, any candidate can match iff it can be reduced (by choosing its free constants) to:
\[
\alpha P^{1/3}+\beta P+\gamma P^2
\]
with \(\alpha=A,\ \beta=2A,\ \gamma=-A/39.01184604772507\), and all other non-polynomial/non-\(P\)-only parts must be removable (set to 0).

Now check candidates:

1. \(c0 P^{1/3}+c1 P^2+c2 P + P c3\sin(\cdot)\). Set \(c3=0\). Then match by choosing \(c0=A,\ c2=2A,\ c1=-A/39.01184604772507\). **Matches**.
2. Has \(P c2\max(0,P+c3)\) (piecewise, generally \(P^2\) only on part of domain) plus sine and constant. To equal a global polynomial for all \(P\), must set \(c2=0\), sine coeff \(c4=0\), and \(c7=0\). Then left with only \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P\), missing \(P^2\). **No**.
3. Same issue as (2) with cos. **No**.
4. Has \(P\max(\cdot)\) and a \(\log(\cdot)\sin(\cdot)\) term. To remove non-polynomial parts need \(c2=0\) and \(c5=0\); then only \(P^{1/3}\), \(P\), and constant \(c4\) (must be 0). Still no \(P^2\). **No**.
5. \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+c2P+Pc3\sin(\cdot)+Pc6\). Set \(c3=0\). Combine linear terms: \(P(c2+c6)\). Choose \(c0=A,\ c1=-A/39.0118...,\ c2+c6=2A\). **Matches**.
6. \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+c2P+c3\sin(\cdot)\). To remove \(t\)-dependence set \(c3=0\). Then choose \(c0,c1,c2\) as above. **Matches**.
7. Contains \(P c1 e^{Pc2}\) (non-polynomial in \(P\) unless \(c1=0\) or \(c2=0\)). If \(c2=0\), term becomes \(Pc1\) (ok). Then expression is \(P(c0+c1)+c4 P^{c3}+c5\). Need \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P^2\) simultaneously but only one power term \(P^{c3}\). Can’t get both. **No**.
8. Has \(c3 e^{c4 t}\log(Pc5+1)\). To remove \(t\) dependence set \(c3=0\) (or \(c4=0\) still leaves log). Then only \(P^{1/3},P^2,P\) remain: choose \(c0=A,\ c1=-A/39.0118...,\ c2=2A\). **Matches**.
9. Has \(c4 P^{c3} e^{c5 t}\). To remove \(t\) dependence need \(c4=0\) or \(c5=0\). If \(c5=0\), term is \(c4P^{c3}\) (a single power). But candidate already has \(P^{1/3},P^2,P\) so we can set \(c4=0\) and match via \(c0,c1,c2\). **Matches**.
10. Has extra \(P^2 c2 e^{c3 t}\). To avoid \(t\) dependence set \(c2=0\) (or \(c3=0\) makes it just another \(P^2\) term). Either way we can match: simplest set \(c3=0\) so it’s \(P^2(c1+c2)\). Choose \(c0=A,\ c4=2A,\ c1+c2=-A/39.0118...\). **Matches**.
11. Has \(P\max(\cdot)\) and \(c4 e^{c5 t}\). Need \(c4=0\) and \(c2=0\) to remove non-polynomial/piecewise. Then no \(P^2\). **No**.
12. Has \(P\max(\cdot)\) and \(P^{c4}c5 e^{c6 t}\). Remove \(t\) dependence by \(c5=0\) (or \(c6=0\) still leaves extra power). Also must set \(c2=0\) to avoid piecewise. Then no \(P^2\). **No**.
13. Has \(P^2 c1 e^{c2 t}\) and \(P c4\max(\cdot)\) plus extra linear terms and constant. To match polynomial for all \(P,t\): set \(c2=0\) so \(P^2\) term is constant-coefficient; set \(c4=0\) to remove Max; set \(c7=0\). Then expression becomes \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+P(c3+c6)\). Choose \(c0=A,\ c1=-A/39.0118...,\ c3+c6=2A\). **Matches**.
14. Has \(P^2 c0 e^{c1 t}\) (remove \(t\): set \(c1=0\)), plus two power terms \(c4P^{c3}+c6P^{c5}\) and constant. We need exactly one \(P^{1/3}\) and no extra powers: set one of those to \(P^{1/3}\) with correct coeff and set the other coeff 0; set constant 0. Then also need linear \(P\) term: already has \(P c2\). Works. Example: set \(c1=0\), \(c0=-A/39.0118...\), \(c2=2A\), choose \(c3=1/3,c4=A\), set \(c6=0\), \(c7=0\). **Matches**.
15. Has extra \(c3 e^{c4 t}\). Must set \(c3=0\). Then match via \(c0,c1,c2\). **Matches**.
16. Has extra \(P c3 (c4+t)^{c5}\) (depends on \(t\) unless \(c3=0\)). Set \(c3=0\). Then match via \(c0,c1,c2\). **Matches**.
17. Has \(P\max(\cdot)\) and \(c4 t^{c5}\). To remove \(t\) dependence set \(c4=0\); to remove Max set \(c2=0\). Then no \(P^2\). **No**.
18. Has rational-in-\(t\) terms. To remove \(t\) dependence set \(c3=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then match via \(c0,c1,c2\). **Matches**.
19. Similar: set \(c3=0,c6=0\). Then match via \(c0,c1,c2\). **Matches**.
20. Has \(P^{c2}P^{c3}c4 = c4 P^{c2+c3}\) plus \(P^{c2}c5\) and \(c6/(c7+t)\). Need no \(t\): set \(c6=0\). We need both \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P^2\) and \(P\). But structure gives \(P^2\) term from \(P^2 c0\), \(P\) from \(Pc1\), and two terms sharing exponent \(c2\) (one is \(P^{c2}\), other is \(P^{c2+c3}\)). Can set \(c2=1/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\) via \(c5\), and set \(c2+c3\) to something we can kill by \(c4=0\). Works: choose \(c4=0\), \(c5=A\), \(c2=1/3\), \(c0=-A/39.0118...\), \(c1=2A\). **Matches**.

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.991*(1 - P/39.01)*P + 0.991*P^(1/3) + 0.991*P`

Let me simplify the GT:
- `0.991*(P - P²/39.01) + 0.991*P^(1/3) + 0.991*P`
- `= 0.991*P - 0.991*P²/39.01 + 0.991*P^(1/3) + 0.991*P`
- `= 0.991*P^(1/3) + 0.991*2*P - 0.02540*P²`

So GT = `c_a * P^(1/3) + c_b * P + c_c * P²` where:
- c_a ≈ 0.991
- c_b ≈ 1.982
- c_c ≈ -0.02540

The GT is: **P^(1/3) term + P term + P² term** (no t dependence, no constant term, no other basis functions).

Now I'll check each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*sin(c4*t + c5)`
Set c3=0 → `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2`. This matches GT structure.
**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*Max(0, P+c3) + P*c4*sin(c5*t+c6) + c7`
Set c4=0, c7=0. Then `P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*Max(0, P+c3)`. For P≥0, if c3≥0, Max(0,P+c3)=P+c3, giving P*c2*(P+c3) = c2*P² + c2*c3*P. Total: P^(1/3)*c0 + (c1+c2*c3)*P + c2*P². This matches.
**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** Same as 2 but cos instead of sin. Set c4=0, c7=0. Same analysis.
**Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 4:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*Max(0,P+c3) + c4 + c5*log(P*c6+1)*sin(c7*t+c8)`
Set c5=0, c4=0, and with c3≥0: same as above.
**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 5:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*sin(c4+c5*t) + P*c6`

**Candidate 6:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3*sin(c4*t+c5)`
Set c3=0 → matches.
**Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 7:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(P*c2) + P^c3*c4 + c5`
The exp(P*c2) term: set c1=0, c5=0. Then P*c0 + P^c3*c4. With c3=1/3: P*c0 + c4*P^(1/3). Missing P² term.
Can't set c2=0 because then P*c1*exp(0)=P*c1, giving P*(c0+c1) + P^(1/3)*c4. Still no P².
**Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 8:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)*log(P*c5+1)`
Need c3*exp(c4*t)*log(P*c5+1)=0 for all t,P. Set c3=0. Then matches.
**Candidate 8 verdict: [MATCH]**

Set c4=0 → matches.

**Candidate 18:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3*t/(c4*t+c5) + c6/(c4*t+c5)`
The t-dependent terms: (c3*t + c6)/(c4*t+c5). For this to be constant for all t, need c3/c4 = constant and c6/c5 = same constant, i.e., c3*c5 = c4*c6. Then it equals c3/c4 for all t. But we also need to add this constant. Actually if c3=0 and c6=0, the t-terms vanish. Then matches.
**Candidate 18 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 19 verdict: [MATCH]**

Or set c2=1/3, c2+c3=2 → c3=5/3. Then c4*P² + c5*P^(1/3) + P²*c0 + P*c1 = (c0+c4)*P² + P*c1 + c5*P^(1/3). Matches.

**Candidate 21 verdict: [MATCH]**

The rational terms: (P*c0 + c7)/(P*c1+c2). If c1=0, this becomes (P*c0+c7)/c2 = c0/c2 * P + c7/c2. Then total: c0/c2*P + c7/c2 + P^(c3+c4)*c5 + P^c3*c6. Set c7=0, c3=1/3, c3+c4=2→c4=5/3. Then c0/c2*P + c5*P² + c6*P^(1/3). Matches.
**Candidate 22 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 23:** `P^(c0+c1)*c2 + P^c0*c3 + c4*log(P*c5+1) + c6/(c7+t)`
Set c6=0, c4=0. Then P^(c0+c1)*c2 + P^c0*c3. Only two power-law terms. Need P^(1/3), P, P². That's three distinct basis functions. Can't match with only two power terms.
Wait - could set c0=1/3, c0+c1=1→c1=2/3. Then c2*P + c3*P^(1/3). Missing P². 
Or c0=1/3, c0+c1=2→c1=5/3. Then c2*P² + c3*P^(1/3). Missing P.
Can we use log? c4*log(P*c5+1) ≠ P for all P. No.
**Candidate 23 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 24:** `P*c0*Max(0,P*c1+1) + P^(c2+c3)*c4 + P^c2*c5 + c6/(c7+t)`
Set c6=0. For P≥0 and c1>0: Max(0,P*c1+1) = P*c1+1. So c0*P*(P*c1+1) = c0*c1*P² + c0*P. Then total: c0*c1*P² + c0*P + c4*P^(c2+c3) + c5*P^c2. Set c2=1/3, c3=0: c0*c1*P² + c0*P + (c4+c5)*P^(1/3). Matches.
**Candidate 24 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 25:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3*t^c4`
The t^c4 term: set c3=0 → matches.
**Candidate 25 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 26:** `P*c0/(c1*t+c2) + P^c3*c4 + P^c5*c6 + c7 + c8/(c1*t+c2)`

**Candidate 26 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 27:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P^c3*c4*log(c5*t+1)`
Set c4=0 → matches.
**Candidate 27 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 28:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3*log(c4*t+1)`
Set c3=0 → matches.

Need c3*t*(P+c4)^c5 = 0 for all t,P. Set c3=0. Matches.

c5*t term: must set c5=0. Then c4=0, c3≥0 → matches.

**Candidate 33:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3*t/(P*c4+c5) + c6/(P*c4+c5)`
The terms (c3*t+c6)/(P*c4+c5) depend on both t and P. To eliminate t-dependence, set c3=0. Then c6/(P*c4+c5). This is a function of P. If c4=0: c6/c5 = constant, set to 0 by c6=0. Then matches.
**Candidate 33 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 34:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)*|P|^c5`
Set c3=0, c2=0. Then P²*c0 + P*c1. Missing P^(1/3). Can't match.
Wait, with P≥0, |P|^c5 = P^c5. Set c4=0: c3*P^c5. Set c5=1/3: P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2 + c3*P^(1/3). Set c2=0. Matches!
**Candidate 34 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 35:** `P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P^c2*c3 + P^c4*c5 + c6`
Set c0=0 (or c1=0). If c1=0: P*c0 + P^c2*c3 + P^c4*c5 + c6. Set c2=1/3, c4=2, c6=0: P*c0 + c3*P^(1/3) + c5*P² + 0. Matches.

= P^(1/3)*c0 + (c1+c2+c3)*P² + (c4+c5)*P. Matches.
**Candidate 48 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 49:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*Max(0,P*c2+1) + P*c3`
For P≥0 and c2>0: Max(0,P*c2+1) = P*c2+1. So c1*P*(c2*P+1) = c1*c2*P² + c1*P. Total: P^(1/3)*c0 + c1*c2*P² + (c1+c3)*P. Matches.
But what if c2<0? For small P, P*c2+1 could still be positive. For large P, it becomes negative. Then Max(0,...) = 0 for large P, which breaks the polynomial structure. But we can choose c2>0 (or c2=0 giving just P*c1+P*c3, missing P²). With c2>0, it works for all P≥0.
**Candidate 49 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 50:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3`
= P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + (c2+c3)*P. Matches.
